<p><b>Debian</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-debfaq-def_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debfaq-def-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Unix-like" title="Unix-like">Unix-like</a> computer <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a> that is composed entirely of <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free software</a>, most of which is under the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">GNU General Public License</a>, and packaged by a group of individuals known as the Debian Project. Three main branches are offered: <i>Stable</i>, <i>Testing</i> and <i>Unstable</i>.</p>
<p>The Debian <i>Stable</i> distribution is one of the most popular for <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Network_server" title="Network server" class="mw-redirect">network servers</a>, and has been used as a base for several other Linux distributions. The Debian <i>Testing</i> and <i>Unstable</i> branches are <a href="/wiki/Rolling_release" title="Rolling release">rolling release</a> and eventually become the <i>stable</i> distribution after development and testing (<i>Unstable</i> becomes <i>Testing</i>, and <i>Testing</i> becomes <i>Stable</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Debian was first announced in 1993 by <a href="/wiki/Ian_Murdock" title="Ian Murdock">Ian Murdock</a>, and the first <i>stable</i> release was made in 1996. The development is carried out over the Internet by a team of volunteers guided by a project leader and three foundational documents: the <a href="/wiki/Debian_Social_Contract" title="Debian Social Contract">Debian Social Contract</a>, the Debian Constitution, and the <a href="/wiki/Debian_Free_Software_Guidelines" title="Debian Free Software Guidelines">Debian Free Software Guidelines</a>. New distributions are updated continually, and the next candidate is released after a time-based <a href="/wiki/Freeze_(software_engineering)" title="Freeze (software engineering)">freeze</a>.</p>
<p>As one of the earliest Linux distributions, it was envisioned that Debian was to be developed openly in the spirit of the <a href="/wiki/GNU_Project" title="GNU Project">GNU Project</a>. This vision drew the attention and support of the <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">Free Software Foundation</a>, which sponsored the project for one year from November 1994 to November 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon the ending of the sponsorship, the Debian project formed the non-profit organisation <a href="/wiki/Software_in_the_Public_Interest" title="Software in the Public Interest">Software in the Public Interest</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features">Features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian_7_Installer_Language_Selection.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Debian_7_Installer_Language_Selection.png/220px-Debian_7_Installer_Language_Selection.png" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Debian_7_Installer_Language_Selection.png/330px-Debian_7_Installer_Language_Selection.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Debian_7_Installer_Language_Selection.png/440px-Debian_7_Installer_Language_Selection.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="630" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian_Installer_graphical_etch.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Debian_Installer_graphical_etch.png/220px-Debian_Installer_graphical_etch.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Debian_Installer_graphical_etch.png/330px-Debian_Installer_graphical_etch.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Debian_Installer_graphical_etch.png/440px-Debian_Installer_graphical_etch.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian_Installer_graphical_etch.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Graphical version of the Debian Installer</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian_6.0_Console_Login.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Debian_6.0_Console_Login.png/220px-Debian_6.0_Console_Login.png" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Debian_6.0_Console_Login.png/330px-Debian_6.0_Console_Login.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Debian_6.0_Console_Login.png/440px-Debian_6.0_Console_Login.png 2x" data-file-width="730" data-file-height="430" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian_6.0_Console_Login.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Debian console login and welcome message</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Debian has access to online repositories that contain over 43,000 <a href="/wiki/Package_(package_management_system)" title="Package (package management system)" class="mw-redirect">software packages</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> making it one of the largest software compilations.<sup id="cite_ref-measuring-lenny_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-measuring-lenny-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian officially contains only free software, but non-free software can be downloaded from the Debian repositories and installed.<sup id="cite_ref-packages_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-packages-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian includes popular free programs such as <a href="/wiki/LibreOffice" title="LibreOffice">LibreOffice</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Corporation_software_rebranded_by_the_Debian_project" title="Mozilla Corporation software rebranded by the Debian project">Iceweasel (Firefox)</a> web browser, <a href="/wiki/Evolution_(software)" title="Evolution (software)">Evolution</a> mail, <a href="/wiki/K3b" title="K3b">K3b</a> disc burner, <a href="/wiki/VLC_media_player" title="VLC media player">VLC media player</a>, <a href="/wiki/GIMP" title="GIMP">GIMP</a> image editor and <a href="/wiki/Evince" title="Evince">Evince</a> document viewer.<sup id="cite_ref-packages_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-packages-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian is a popular choice for <a href="/wiki/Web_server" title="Web server">web servers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The cost of developing all of the packages included in Debian 5.0 Lenny (323 million lines of code) has been estimated to be about <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>&#160;8 billion</span>, using one method based on the <a href="/wiki/COCOMO" title="COCOMO">COCOMO</a> model.<sup id="cite_ref-measuring-lenny_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-measuring-lenny-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Ohloh" title="Ohloh" class="mw-redirect">Ohloh</a> estimates that the <a href="/wiki/Codebase" title="Codebase">codebase</a> (78 million lines of code) would cost about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$&#160;1.5 billion</span> to develop, using a different method based on the same model.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The current stable release, Debian 8.2 code-named Jessie, is officially supported on ten <a href="#Architecture_ports">architecture ports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable changes in this release include using <a href="/wiki/Systemd" title="Systemd">systemd</a> as the default <a href="/wiki/Init" title="Init">init</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-debian_systemd_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian_systemd-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kernels">Kernels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Kernels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Debian supports <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> officially, offered <a href="/wiki/Debian_GNU/kFreeBSD" title="Debian GNU/kFreeBSD">kFreeBSD</a> for version 7 but not 8,<sup id="cite_ref-new-in-7_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new-in-7-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/GNU_Hurd" title="GNU Hurd">GNU Hurd</a> unofficially.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> GNU/kFreeBSD was released as a technology preview for <a href="/wiki/IA-32" title="IA-32">IA-32</a> and <a href="/wiki/X86-64" title="X86-64">x86-64</a> <a href="/wiki/Computer_architecture" title="Computer architecture">architectures</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-new-in-7_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new-in-7-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> and lacked the amount of software available in Debian's Linux distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Official support for kFreeBSD was removed for version 8, which did not provide a kFreeBSD-based distribution.</p>
<p>There are several flavors of the Linux kernel for each port; for instance, the i386 port has flavors for IA-32 <a href="/wiki/IBM_PC_compatible" title="IBM PC compatible">PCs</a> supporting <a href="/wiki/Physical_Address_Extension" title="Physical Address Extension">Physical Address Extension</a> and <a href="/wiki/Real-time_computing" title="Real-time computing">real-time computing</a>, for older PCs, and for x86-64 PCs.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The Linux kernel does not officially contain <a href="/wiki/Firmware" title="Firmware">firmware</a> without sources, although such firmware is available in non-free packages and alternative installation media.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Installation_and_Live_images">Installation and Live images</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Installation and Live images">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Debian offers DVD and CD <a href="/wiki/ISO_image" title="ISO image">images</a> for installation that can be downloaded using <a href="/wiki/BitTorrent_(protocol)" title="BitTorrent (protocol)" class="mw-redirect">BitTorrent</a> or <a href="/wiki/Jigdo" title="Jigdo">jigdo</a>. Physical disks can also be bought from retailers.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The full sets are made up of several discs (the amd64 port consists of 10 DVDs or 69 CDs),<sup id="cite_ref-jigdo-cd_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jigdo-cd-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> but only the first disc is required for installation, as the installer can retrieve software not contained in the first disc image from online repositories.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Debian offers different network installation methods. A minimal install of Debian is available via the "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Netinst&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Netinst (page does not exist)">netinst</a>" CD, whereby Debian is installed with just a base and later additional software can be downloaded from the Internet. Another option is to boot the installer from the network.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Installation images are <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_disc" title="Hybrid disc">hybrid</a> on some architectures and can be used to create a <a href="/wiki/Booting" title="Booting">bootable</a> USB drive (<a href="/wiki/Live_USB" title="Live USB">Live USB</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The default desktop may be chosen from the DVD boot menu among <a href="/wiki/GNOME" title="GNOME">GNOME</a>, <a href="/wiki/KDE_Software_Compilation" title="KDE Software Compilation">KDE Software Compilation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xfce" title="Xfce">Xfce</a> and <a href="/wiki/LXDE" title="LXDE">LXDE</a>, and from special disc 1 CDs.<sup id="cite_ref-installation-7-6.3_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-installation-7-6.3-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wheezy-hands-on_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wheezy-hands-on-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Desktop_environments">Desktop environments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Desktop environments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Docky_on_Gnome_Shell_of_Gnome_3,_Debian_GNU-Linux.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Docky_on_Gnome_Shell_of_Gnome_3%2C_Debian_GNU-Linux.png/220px-Docky_on_Gnome_Shell_of_Gnome_3%2C_Debian_GNU-Linux.png" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Docky_on_Gnome_Shell_of_Gnome_3%2C_Debian_GNU-Linux.png/330px-Docky_on_Gnome_Shell_of_Gnome_3%2C_Debian_GNU-Linux.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Docky_on_Gnome_Shell_of_Gnome_3%2C_Debian_GNU-Linux.png/440px-Docky_on_Gnome_Shell_of_Gnome_3%2C_Debian_GNU-Linux.png 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Docky_on_Gnome_Shell_of_Gnome_3,_Debian_GNU-Linux.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Docky" title="Docky" class="mw-redirect">docky</a> on Gnome Shell of Gnome 3, Debian</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian-kde.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Debian-kde.png/220px-Debian-kde.png" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Debian-kde.png/330px-Debian-kde.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Debian-kde.png/440px-Debian-kde.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian-kde.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Debian KDE desktop</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Debian offers CD images specifically built for GNOME (the default in Wheezy), KDE Software Compilation, Xfce and LXDE.<sup id="cite_ref-squeeze_released_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-squeeze_released-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MATE_(desktop_environment)" title="MATE (desktop environment)" class="mw-redirect">MATE</a> is officially supported,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon_(software)" title="Cinnamon (software)">Cinnamon</a> support was added with Debian 8.0 Jessie.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Less common <a href="/wiki/Window_manager" title="Window manager">window managers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_(window_manager)" title="Enlightenment (window manager)" class="mw-redirect">Enlightenment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Openbox" title="Openbox">Openbox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fluxbox" title="Fluxbox">Fluxbox</a>, <a href="/wiki/IceWM" title="IceWM">IceWM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Window_Maker" title="Window Maker">Window Maker</a> and others are available.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The default desktop environment of version 7.0 Wheezy was temporarily switched to Xfce, because GNOME 3 did not fit on the first CD of the set.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The default for the version 8.0 Jessie was changed again to Xfce in November 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> and back to GNOME in September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Debian_Live">Debian Live</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Debian Live">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Debian releases <a href="/wiki/Live_CD" title="Live CD">live install</a> images for CDs, DVDs and USB thumb drives, for <a href="/wiki/IA-32" title="IA-32">IA-32</a> and <a href="/wiki/X86-64" title="X86-64">x86-64</a> architectures, and with a choice of desktop environments. These "Debian Live" images allow the user to boot from removable media and run Debian without affecting the contents of their computer.</p>
<p>A full install of Debian to the computer's hard drive can be initiated from the live image environment.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Personalized images can be built with the live-build tool for discs, USB drives and for <a href="/wiki/Network_booting" title="Network booting">network booting</a> purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Package_management">Package management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Package management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Package_management_system" title="Package management system" class="mw-redirect">Package management</a> operations can be performed with different tools available on Debian, from the lowest level command <em>dpkg</em> to graphical front-ends like Synaptic. The recommended standard for administering packages on a Debian system is the <em>apt</em> toolset.<sup id="cite_ref-deb-ref-2_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deb-ref-2-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dpkg" title="Dpkg">dpkg</a> provides the low-level infrastructure for package management.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The dpkg database contains the list of installed software on the current system. The dpkg command tool does not know about repositories. The command can work with local <a href="/wiki/Deb_(file_format)" title="Deb (file format)">.deb</a> package files as well as information from the dpkg database.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="APT_tools">APT tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: APT tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian_7_Aptitude_Package_Details.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Debian_7_Aptitude_Package_Details.png/220px-Debian_7_Aptitude_Package_Details.png" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Debian_7_Aptitude_Package_Details.png/330px-Debian_7_Aptitude_Package_Details.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Debian_7_Aptitude_Package_Details.png/440px-Debian_7_Aptitude_Package_Details.png 2x" data-file-width="730" data-file-height="430" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian_7_Aptitude_Package_Details.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Using Aptitude to view Debian package details</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian-aptitude.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Debian-aptitude.png/220px-Debian-aptitude.png" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Debian-aptitude.png/330px-Debian-aptitude.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Debian-aptitude.png/440px-Debian-aptitude.png 2x" data-file-width="661" data-file-height="482" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian-aptitude.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Package installed with Aptitude</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Packaging_Tool" title="Advanced Packaging Tool">APT</a> tool allows administration of an installed Debian system for retrieving and resolving package <a href="/wiki/Coupling_(computer_programming)" title="Coupling (computer programming)">dependencies</a> from <a href="/wiki/Software_repository" title="Software repository">repositories</a>. APT tools share dependency information and cached packages.<sup id="cite_ref-deb-ref-2_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deb-ref-2-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aptitude_(software)" title="Aptitude (software)">Aptitude</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Command_line" title="Command line" class="mw-redirect">command line</a> tool that also offers a <a href="/wiki/Text-based_user_interface" title="Text-based user interface">text-based user interface</a>. The program comes with enhancements such as better search on package <a href="/wiki/Metadata" title="Metadata">metadata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-deb-ref-2_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deb-ref-2-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><em>apt-get</em> and <em>apt-cache</em> are command tools of the standard <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Packaging_Tool#Usage" title="Advanced Packaging Tool">apt</a> package. apt-get installs and removes packages, and apt-cache is used for searching packages and displaying package information.<sup id="cite_ref-deb-ref-2_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deb-ref-2-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="GDebi_and_other_front-ends"><span id="GDEBI"></span>GDebi and other front-ends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: GDebi and other front-ends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p><a href="/wiki/GDebi" title="GDebi" class="mw-redirect">GDebi</a> is an APT tool which can be used in command-line and on the GUI.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> GDebi can install a local .deb file via the command line like the dpkg command, but with access to repositories to resolve dependencies.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Other graphical front-ends for APT include <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_Software_Center" title="Ubuntu Software Center">Software Center</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Synaptic_(software)" title="Synaptic (software)">Synaptic</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Apper" title="Apper">Apper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Branches">Branches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Branches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian-cd-cover1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Debian-cd-cover1.png/220px-Debian-cd-cover1.png" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Debian-cd-cover1.png/330px-Debian-cd-cover1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Debian-cd-cover1.png/440px-Debian-cd-cover1.png 2x" data-file-width="812" data-file-height="547" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Debian-cd-cover1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Debian 4.0 Etch box cover</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Three <a href="/wiki/Branching_(revision_control)" title="Branching (revision control)" class="mw-redirect">branches</a> of Debian (also called <em>releases</em>, <em>distributions</em> or <em>suites</em>) are regularly maintained:<sup id="cite_ref-debian-releases_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-releases-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><i>Stable</i> is the current release and targets stable and well-tested software needs.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Stable</i> is made by freezing <i>Testing</i> for a few months where bugs are fixed and packages with too many bugs are removed; then the resulting system is released as <i>Stable</i>. It is updated only if major security or usability fixes are incorporated.<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> This branch has an optional <a href="/wiki/Backporting" title="Backporting">backports</a> service that provides more recent versions of some software.<sup id="cite_ref-news-backports-official_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news-backports-official-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Stable</i> '​s CDs and DVDs can be found in the Debian website.<sup id="cite_ref-jigdo-cd_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jigdo-cd-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Testing</i> is the preview branch that will eventually become the next major release. The packages included in this branch have had some testing in <i>Unstable</i> but they may not be fit for release yet. It contains newer packages than <i>Stable</i> but older than <i>Unstable</i>. This branch is updated continually until it is frozen.<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Testing</i> '​s CDs and DVDs can be found on the Debian website.<sup id="cite_ref-jigdo-cd_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jigdo-cd-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Unstable</i>, always codenamed <i>Sid</i>, is the <a href="/wiki/Trunk_(software)" title="Trunk (software)">trunk</a>. Packages are accepted without checking the distribution as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> This branch is usually run by software developers who participate in a project and need the latest libraries available, and by those who prefer <a href="/wiki/Bleeding_edge_technology" title="Bleeding edge technology">bleeding-edge</a> software.<sup id="cite_ref-debian-releases_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-releases-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian does not provide Sid installation discs. This branch can be installed through a system upgrade from <i>Testing</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Other branches in Debian:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Oldstable</i> is the prior <i>Stable</i> release.<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> It is supported by the Debian Security Team until one year after a new <i>Stable</i> is released, and since the release of Debian 6, for an additional 2 years through the Long Term Support project.<sup id="cite_ref-securityfaq_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-securityfaq-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Eventually, <i>Oldstable</i> is moved to a repository for archived releases.<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Oldoldstable</i> is the prior <i>Oldstable</i> release. It is supported by the Long Term Support community. Eventually, <i>Oldoldstable</i> is moved to a repository for archived releases.</li>
<li><i>Experimental</i> is a temporary staging area of highly experimental software that is likely to break the system. It is not a full distribution and missing dependencies are commonly found in <i>Unstable</i>, where new software without the damage chance is normally uploaded.<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The <em>snapshot</em> archive provides older versions of the branches. They may be used to install a specific older version of some software.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Numbering_scheme">Numbering scheme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Numbering scheme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Stable</i> and <i>Oldstable</i> get minor updates, called <em>point releases</em>; as of September 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <i>Stable</i> release is version 8.2,<sup id="cite_ref-jessie-changelog_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jessie-changelog-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <i>Oldstable</i> release is version 7.9.<sup id="cite_ref-wheezy-changelog_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wheezy-changelog-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The numbering scheme for the point releases up to Debian 4.0 was to include the letter <i>r</i> (for <i>revision</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-hertzog-1.6_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hertzog-1.6-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> after the main version number and then the number of the point release; for example, the latest point release of version 4.0 is 4.0r9.<sup id="cite_ref-etch-release_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etch-release-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> This scheme was chosen because a new dotted version would make the old one look obsolete and vendors would have trouble selling their CDs.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From Debian 5.0, the numbering scheme of point releases was changed, conforming to the GNU version numbering standard;<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> the first point release of Debian 5.0 was 5.0.1 instead of 5.0r1.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The numbering scheme was once again changed for the first Debian 7 update, which was version 7.1.<sup id="cite_ref-wheezy-changelog_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wheezy-changelog-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>r</i> scheme is no longer in use, but point release announcements include a note about not throwing away old CDs.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Code_names">Code names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Code names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The code names of Debian releases are <a href="/wiki/List_of_Toy_Story_characters" title="List of Toy Story characters">names of characters</a> from the <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_(franchise)" title="Toy Story (franchise)">Toy Story</a></i> films. Debian 8 was named Jessie, after the <a href="/wiki/Jessie_(Toy_Story)" title="Jessie (Toy Story)">cowgirl</a> in <i>Toy Story 2</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_3" title="Toy Story 3">Toy Story 3</a></i>. The <i>Testing</i> branch is currently named Stretch, after the <a href="/wiki/Stretch_(Toy_Story)" title="Stretch (Toy Story)" class="mw-redirect">toy rubber octopus</a> in <i>Toy Story 3</i>. The <i>Unstable</i> trunk is permanently nicknamed <a href="/wiki/Sid_(Toy_Story)" title="Sid (Toy Story)" class="mw-redirect">Sid</a>, after the emotionally unstable <a href="/wiki/Boy_next_door" title="Boy next door">boy next door</a> who regularly destroyed toys.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>This naming tradition came about because <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Perens" title="Bruce Perens">Bruce Perens</a> was involved in the early development of Debian while working at <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHertzog20139_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHertzog20139-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Blends">Blends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Blends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Debian_Pure_Blend" title="Debian Pure Blend">Debian Pure Blends</a> are subsets of a Debian release configured out-of-the-box for users with particular skills and interests.<sup id="cite_ref-debian-pure-blends_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-pure-blends-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> For instance, Debian Jr. is targeted at children, while <a href="/wiki/Debian_Science" title="Debian Science" class="mw-redirect">Debian Science</a> aims at researchers and scientists.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The complete Debian distribution includes all available Debian Pure Blends.<sup id="cite_ref-debian-pure-blends_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-pure-blends-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> "Debian Blend" (without "Pure") is a term for a Debian-based distribution that strives to become part of mainstream Debian, and have its extra features included in future releases.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Debian "swirl" logo was designed by Raul Silva<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> in 1999 as part of a contest to replace the semi-official logo that had been used.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The winner of the contest received an @debian.org <a href="/wiki/Email_address" title="Email address">email address</a>, as well as a set of Debian 2.1 install CDs for the architecture of their choice. There has been no official statement from the Debian project on the logo's meaning, but at the time of the logo's selection, it was suggested that the logo represented the <a href="/wiki/Magic_smoke" title="Magic smoke">magic smoke</a> that made computers work.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>One theory about the origin of the Debian logo is based on an interesting detail: <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Lightyear" title="Buzz Lightyear">Buzz Lightyear</a>, the chosen character for the first named Debian release, has a swirl in his chin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrafft200566_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrafft200566-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Zacchiroli" title="Stefano Zacchiroli">Stefano Zacchiroli</a> also suggested that this swirl is the Debian one.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archive_areas">Archive areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Archive areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Debian_Free_Software_Guidelines" title="Debian Free Software Guidelines">Debian Free Software Guidelines</a> (DFSG) define the distinctive meaning of the word "free" as in "<a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-socialcontract_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-socialcontract-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Packages which comply with these guidelines, usually under the GNU General Public License, <a href="/wiki/BSD_licenses" title="BSD licenses">Modified BSD License</a> or <a href="/wiki/Artistic_License" title="Artistic License">Artistic License</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> are included inside the <em>main</em> area;<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> otherwise, they are included inside the <em>non-free</em> and <em>contrib</em> areas. These last two areas are not distributed within the official installation media, but they can be adopted manually.<sup id="cite_ref-socialcontract_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-socialcontract-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Non-free includes packages which do not comply with the DFSG,<sup id="cite_ref-debian-policy_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-policy-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> such as documentation with invariant sections and <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary software</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> and legally questionable packages.<sup id="cite_ref-debian-policy_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-policy-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Contrib includes packages which do comply with the DFSG but fail other requirements; for instance, they may depend on packages which are in non-free or requires such for building them.<sup id="cite_ref-debian-policy_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-policy-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Richard_Stallman" title="Richard Stallman">Richard Stallman</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">Free Software Foundation</a> have criticized the Debian project for hosting the non-free repository and because the contrib and non-free areas are easily accessible,<sup id="cite_ref-fsf_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fsf-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> an opinion echoed by some in Debian including the former project leader Wichert Akkerman.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The internal dissent in the Debian project regarding the non-free section has persisted,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> but the last time it came to a vote in 2004, the majority decided to keep it.<sup id="cite_ref-nonfreeremovalvote_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nonfreeremovalvote-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multimedia_support">Multimedia support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Multimedia support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Multimedia support has been problematic in Debian regarding <a href="/wiki/Codec" title="Codec">codecs</a> threatened by possible patent infringements, without sources or under too restrictive licenses,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> and regarding technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Adobe Flash</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lenny_released_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lenny_released-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Even though packages with problems related to their distribution could go into the non-free area, software such as <a href="/wiki/Libdvdcss" title="Libdvdcss">libdvdcss</a> is not hosted at Debian.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There is a notable third party repository, formerly known as debian-multimedia.org,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> providing software not present in Debian such as <a href="/wiki/Windows_API" title="Windows API">Windows</a> codecs, libdvdcss and the <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Even though this repository is maintained by Christian Marillat, a Debian developer, it is not part of the project and is not hosted on a Debian server. The repository provides packages already included in Debian, interfering with the official maintenance. Eventually, project leader Stefano Zacchiroli asked Marillat to either settle an agreement about the packaging or to stop using the "Debian" name.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Marillat chose the latter and renamed the repository to deb-multimedia.org. The repository was so popular that the switchover was announced by the official blog of the Debian project.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hardware_support">Hardware support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hardware support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hardware_requirements">Hardware requirements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hardware requirements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Hardware requirements are at least those of the kernel and the <a href="/wiki/GNU" title="GNU">GNU</a> toolsets. Debian supports <a href="/wiki/Uniprocessor_system" title="Uniprocessor system">uniprocessor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Symmetric_multiprocessor_system" title="Symmetric multiprocessor system">symmetric multiprocessor systems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hreqs2_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hreqs2-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian's recommended system requirements depend on the level of installation, which corresponds to increased numbers of installed components:<sup id="cite_ref-hreqs1_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hreqs1-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
<tr>
<th>Type</th>
<th>Minimum <a href="/wiki/Random-access_memory" title="Random-access memory">RAM</a> size</th>
<th>Recommended RAM size</th>
<th>Minimum processor clock speed (IA-32)</th>
<th>Hard drive capacity</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Non desktop</td>
<td>64&#160;<a href="/wiki/Megabyte" title="Megabyte">MB</a></td>
<td>256&#160;MB</td>
<td></td>
<td>1&#160;<a href="/wiki/Gigabyte" title="Gigabyte">GB</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Desktop</td>
<td>128&#160;MB</td>
<td>512&#160;MB</td>
<td>1&#160;GHz</td>
<td>5&#160;GB</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The real minimum memory requirements depend on the architecture and may be much less than the numbers listed in this table. It is possible to install Debian with 60&#160;<a href="/wiki/Megabyte" title="Megabyte">MB</a> of RAM for x86-64;<sup id="cite_ref-hreqs1_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hreqs1-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> the installer will run in low memory mode and it is recommended to create a <a href="/wiki/Paging" title="Paging">swap partition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-installation-7-6.3_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-installation-7-6.3-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The installer for <a href="/wiki/Z/Architecture" title="Z/Architecture">z/Architecture</a> requires about 20&#160;MB of RAM, but relies on network hardware.<sup id="cite_ref-hreqs1_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hreqs1-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Similarly, disk space requirements, which depend on the packages to be installed, can be reduced by manually selecting the packages needed.<sup id="cite_ref-hreqs1_92-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hreqs1-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> As of August 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there is no Pure Blend that would lower the hardware requirements easily.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It is possible to run <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">graphical user interfaces</a> on older or low-end systems, but the installation of <a href="/wiki/Window_manager" title="Window manager">window managers</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Desktop_environment" title="Desktop environment">desktop environments</a> is recommended, as desktop environments are more resource-intensive. Requirements for individual software vary widely and must be considered as well as those of the base operating environment.<sup id="cite_ref-hreqs1_92-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hreqs1-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture_ports">Architecture ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Architecture ports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

</div>
</div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_ports">Official ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Official ports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>As of the Jessie release<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the official ports are:<sup id="cite_ref-packages_base-files_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-packages_base-files-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><em>amd64</em>: <a href="/wiki/X86-64" title="X86-64">x86-64</a> architecture with 64-bit userland and supporting 32-bit software</li>
<li><em>arm64</em>: ARMv8-A architecture<sup id="cite_ref-two-ports_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-two-ports-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><em>armel</em>: Little-<a href="/wiki/Endianness" title="Endianness">endian</a> <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">ARM architecture</a> (ARMv4T instruction set)<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> on various embedded systems (<a href="/wiki/EABI" title="EABI" class="mw-redirect">EABI</a>)</li>
<li><em>armhf</em>: ARM hard-float architecture (ARMv7 instruction set) requiring hardware with a <a href="/wiki/Floating-point_unit" title="Floating-point unit">floating-point unit</a></li>
<li><em>i386</em>: <a href="/wiki/IA-32" title="IA-32">IA-32</a> architecture with 32-bit userland, compatible with x86-64 machines<sup id="cite_ref-hreqs2_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hreqs2-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><em>mips</em>: Big-endian <a href="/wiki/MIPS_architecture" title="MIPS architecture" class="mw-redirect">MIPS architecture</a></li>
<li><em>mipsel</em>: Little-endian MIPS architecture</li>
<li><em>powerpc</em>: <a href="/wiki/PowerPC" title="PowerPC">PowerPC</a> architecture</li>
<li><em>ppc64el</em>: Little-endian PowerPC64 architecture supporting <a href="/wiki/POWER7" title="POWER7">POWER7+</a> and <a href="/wiki/POWER8" title="POWER8">POWER8</a> CPUs<sup id="cite_ref-two-ports_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-two-ports-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><em>s390x</em>: z/Architecture with 64-bit userland, intended to replace <em>s390</em><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Unofficial_ports">Unofficial ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Unofficial ports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Unofficial ports are available as part of the <i>Unstable</i> distribution:<sup id="cite_ref-packages_base-files_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-packages_base-files-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><em>alpha</em>: <a href="/wiki/DEC_Alpha" title="DEC Alpha">DEC Alpha</a> architecture</li>
<li><em>hppa</em>: HP <a href="/wiki/PA-RISC" title="PA-RISC">PA-RISC</a> architecture</li>
<li><em>hurd-i386</em>: <a href="/wiki/GNU_Hurd" title="GNU Hurd">GNU Hurd</a> kernel on <a href="/wiki/IA-32" title="IA-32">IA-32</a> architecture</li>
<li><em>kfreebsd-amd64</em>: Kernel of <a href="/wiki/FreeBSD" title="FreeBSD">FreeBSD</a> on x86-64 architecture</li>
<li><em>kfreebsd-i386</em>: Kernel of FreeBSD on IA-32 architecture</li>
<li><em>m68k</em>: <a href="/wiki/Motorola_68000_family" title="Motorola 68000 family" class="mw-redirect">Motorola 68k</a> architecture on <a href="/wiki/Amiga" title="Amiga">Amiga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atari_ST" title="Atari ST">Atari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macintosh" title="Macintosh">Macintosh</a> and various embedded <a href="/wiki/VMEbus" title="VMEbus">VME</a> systems</li>
<li><em>powerpcspe</em>: <a href="/wiki/PowerPC_e500" title="PowerPC e500">PowerPCSPE</a> architecture, incompatible with <a href="/wiki/PowerPC" title="PowerPC">PowerPC</a></li>
<li><em>ppc64</em>: <a href="/wiki/Ppc64" title="Ppc64">PowerPC64</a> architecture supporting 64-bit PowerPC CPUs with <a href="/wiki/AltiVec" title="AltiVec">VMX</a></li>
<li><em>sh4</em>: Hitachi <a href="/wiki/SuperH" title="SuperH">SuperH</a> architecture</li>
<li><em>sparc64</em>: Sun <a href="/wiki/SPARC" title="SPARC">SPARC</a> architecture with 64-bit userland</li>
<li><em>x32</em>: <a href="/wiki/X32_ABI" title="X32 ABI">x32 ABI</a> userland for x86-64<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Embedded_systems"><span id="EMBEDDED"></span>Embedded systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Embedded systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Debian supports a variety of <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">ARM</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Network-attached_storage" title="Network-attached storage">NAS</a> devices. The <a href="/wiki/NSLU2" title="NSLU2">NSLU2</a> was supported by the installer in Debian 4.0 and 5.0,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Michlmayr" title="Martin Michlmayr">Martin Michlmayr</a> is providing installation <a href="/wiki/Tar_(computing)" title="Tar (computing)">tarballs</a> since version 6.0.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Other supported NAS devices are the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_network-attached_storage_series" title="Buffalo network-attached storage series">Buffalo</a> Kurobox Pro,<sup id="cite_ref-new-in-lenny-arm_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new-in-lenny-arm-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> GLAN Tank, Thecus N2100<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> and QNAP Turbo Stations.<sup id="cite_ref-new-in-lenny-arm_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new-in-lenny-arm-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Devices based on the Kirkwood <a href="/wiki/System_on_a_chip" title="System on a chip">SoC</a> are supported too, such as the <a href="/wiki/SheevaPlug" title="SheevaPlug">SheevaPlug</a> plug computer and OpenRD products.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> There are efforts to run Debian on mobile devices, but this is not a project goal yet since the Debian Linux kernel maintainers would not apply the necessary patches.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, there are packages for resource-limited systems.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There are efforts to support Debian on <a href="/wiki/Wireless_access_point" title="Wireless access point">wireless access points</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian is known to run on set-top boxes.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> There is an ongoing work to support the AM335x processor,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> which is used in <a href="/wiki/Point_of_sale" title="Point of sale">electronic point of service</a> solutions.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian may be customized to run on cash machines.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/BeagleBoard" title="BeagleBoard">BeagleBoard</a>, a low-power open-source hardware single-board computer (Produced by Texas Instruments) has switched to Debian Linux pre-loaded on its Beaglebone Black board's flash.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Support_for_communities">Support for communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Support for communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Localization">Localization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Localization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Several parts of Debian are translated into languages other than English, including package descriptions, configuration messages, documentation and the website.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The level of software localization depends on the language, ranging from the highly supported <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> to the hardly translated <a href="/wiki/Muscogee_language" title="Muscogee language">Creek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> The installer is available in 73 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Virtual_communities">Virtual communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Virtual communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Debian provides packages targeted at <a href="/wiki/Virtual_community" title="Virtual community">virtual communities</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> application interfaces are available to programmers;<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Pidgin_(software)" title="Pidgin (software)">Pidgin</a> messaging client used a custom plugin for Facebook until the networking site added support for <a href="/wiki/XMPP" title="XMPP">XMPP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian 5.0 Lenny was the last release supporting <a href="/wiki/Tencent_QQ" title="Tencent QQ">Tencent QQ</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Communication with <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a> is possible using software in the contrib area.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policies">Policies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Policies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Debian is known for its manifesto,<sup id="cite_ref-project-history-debian-manifesto_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-project-history-debian-manifesto-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-debian-turns-20_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-turns-20-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> social contract,<sup id="cite_ref-debian-turns-20_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debian-turns-20-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> and policies.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Debian's policies and team efforts focus on <a href="/wiki/Collaborative_software_development_model" title="Collaborative software development model">collaborative software development and testing processes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-debfaq-def_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debfaq-def-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result of its policies, a new major release tends to occur every two years with revision releases that fix security issues and important problems.<sup id="cite_ref-hertzog-1.6_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hertzog-1.6-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-two-year-cycle_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-two-year-cycle-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbcaption">Simplified organizational structure</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Debian project is a volunteer organization with three foundational documents:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <em><a href="/wiki/Debian_Social_Contract" title="Debian Social Contract">Debian Social Contract</a></em> defines a set of basic principles by which the project and its developers conduct affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-socialcontract_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-socialcontract-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The <em><a href="/wiki/Debian_Free_Software_Guidelines" title="Debian Free Software Guidelines">Debian Free Software Guidelines</a></em> define the criteria for "free software" and thus what software is permissible in the distribution. These guidelines have been adopted as the basis of the <a href="/wiki/The_Open_Source_Definition" title="The Open Source Definition">Open Source Definition</a>. Although this document can be considered separate, it formally is part of the Social Contract.<sup id="cite_ref-socialcontract_72-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-socialcontract-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The <em>Debian Constitution</em> describes the organizational structure for formal decision-making within the project, and enumerates the powers and responsibilities of the Project Leader, the Secretary and other roles.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em;">
<tr>
<th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Historical population</th>
</tr>
<tr style="font-size:95%">
<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th>
<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Debian developers">DD</abbr></th>
<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Percent change">±%</abbr></th>

<p>Debian developers are organized in a <a href="/wiki/Web_of_trust" title="Web of trust">web of trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman2013143_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman2013143-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> There are at present<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> about one thousand active Debian developers,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> but it is possible to contribute to the project without being an official developer.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The project maintains official <a href="/wiki/Mailing_list" title="Mailing list">mailing lists</a> and conferences for communication and coordination between developers.<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> For issues with single packages and other tasks,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> a public <a href="/wiki/Software_bug" title="Software bug">bug</a> tracking system is used by developers and end users. <a href="/wiki/Internet_Relay_Chat" title="Internet Relay Chat">Internet Relay Chat</a> channels (primarily on the <a href="/wiki/Open_and_Free_Technology_Community" title="Open and Free Technology Community">OFTC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freenode" title="Freenode">freenode</a> networks) are also used for communication among developers<sup id="cite_ref-distributions_46-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-distributions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> and to provide real time help.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Debian is supported by donations made to organizations authorized by the leader.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest supporter is <a href="/wiki/Software_in_the_Public_Interest" title="Software in the Public Interest">Software in the Public Interest</a>, the owner of the Debian trademark, manager of the monetary donations<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Umbrella_organization" title="Umbrella organization">umbrella organization</a> for various other community free software projects.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A Project Leader is elected once per year by the developers. The leader has special powers, but they are not absolute, and appoints delegates to perform specialized tasks. Delegates make decisions as they think is best, taking into account technical criteria and consensus. By way of a General Resolution, the developers may recall the leader, reverse a decision made by the leader or a delegate, amend foundational documents and make other binding decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_128-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The voting method is based on the <a href="/wiki/Schulze_method" title="Schulze method">Cloneproof Schwartz Sequential Dropping</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vote-info_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vote-info-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div id="Containerleaders" class="toccolours" style="text-align: left; padding:0.5em 0 0 0; border-style:solid; float:right;clear:right; padding:0 0.5em; margin:0.3em 0 0.8em 1.4em; overflow: hidden;">

<div id="Legendleaders" class="toccolours" style="margin-left:3.1em; border-style:none; float:left; clear:both;"></div>
<div id="Captionleaders" class="toccolours" style="margin:0 0.5em; float:left; padding:0 auto; border-style:none; clear:both; text-align:center; width:14.25em">
<div style="text-align: left">The Project Leader is the public face of Debian and defines its direction.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Project leadership is distributed occasionally. Branden Robinson was helped by the Project <a href="/wiki/Scud_(dog)" title="Scud (dog)" class="mw-redirect">Scud</a>, a team of developers that assisted the leader,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> but there were concerns that such leadership would split Debian into two developer classes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrafft200534_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrafft200534-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Anthony Towns created a supplemental position, Second In Charge (2IC), that shared some powers of the leader.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Steve McIntyre was 2IC and had a 2IC himself.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>One important role in Debian's leadership is that of a <a href="/wiki/Software_release_life_cycle" title="Software release life cycle">release</a> manager.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> The release team sets goals for the next release, supervises the processes and decides when to release. The team is led by the next release managers and stable release managers.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> Release assistants were introduced in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Developer_recruitment.2C_motivation.2C_and_resignation">Developer recruitment, motivation, and resignation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Developer recruitment, motivation, and resignation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Debian project has an influx of applicants wishing to become developers.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> These applicants must undergo a vetting process which establishes their identity, motivation, understanding of the project's principles, and technical competence.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> This process has become much harder throughout the years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHertzog201313_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHertzog201313-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Debian developers join the project for a number of reasons; some that have been cited include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Debian is their main operating system and they want to promote Debian<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>To improve the support for their favorite technology<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>They are involved with a Debian derivative<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>A desire to contribute back to the <a href="/wiki/Free-software_community" title="Free-software community" class="mw-redirect">free-software community</a><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>To make their Debian maintenance work easier<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Debian developers may resign their positions at any time or, when deemed necessary, they can be expelled.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_128-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> Those who follow the retiring protocol are granted the "emeritus" status and they may regain their membership through a shortened new member process.<sup id="cite_ref-developer-duties_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-developer-duties-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_procedures">Development procedures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Development procedures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 25ex;">
